  "content": "# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries](#1-subsystem-purpose-and-boundaries)\n2. [Component Responsibilities](#2-component-responsibilities)\n3. [End-to-End Request Flow](#3-end-to-end-request-flow)\n4. [The Fair Queuing Algorithm in Detail](#4-the-fair-queuing-algorithm-in-detail)\n5. [Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs](#5-failure-modes-limits-and-design-tradeoffs)\n6. [Extension Points and Customization Hooks](#6-extension-points-and-customization-hooks)\n7. [Operational Implications](#7-operational-implications)\n8. [File Map](#8-file-map)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe APF (API Priority and Fairness) QueueSet subsystem implements **Fair Queuing for Server Requests** inside the Kubernetes API server. Its job is to prevent any single client or flow from monopolizing the apiserver's concurrency budget, while still making forward progress for all active flows under overload.\n\nEvery non-exempt apiserver request is routed through a *priority level*, each of which owns exactly one `QueueSet`. The `QueueSet` for a priority level is the gate that decides:\n\n- whether an incoming request can be dispatched immediately (seats available),\n- whether it must wait in a queue (backpressure),\n- whether it must be rejected outright (queue full and concurrency limit exceeded), or\n- whether it times out while waiting (context cancelled).\n\n### Scope Boundary\n\nThe QueueSet subsystem is responsible only for **queuing and dispatch decisions** within a single priority level. It has no knowledge of:\n\n- how requests are classified (FlowSchema matching happens in `apf_controller.go`);\n- cross-level concurrency borrowing (also handled at the controller layer);\n- HTTP-level admission or request routing.\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\n| Dependency | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `configController` (`apf_controller.go`) | Creates and reconfigures QueueSets; provides `ConcurrencyLimit` and queuing parameters |\n| `FlowSchema` / `PriorityLevelConfiguration` API objects | Supply `HandSize`, `Queues`, `QueueLengthLimit`, `NominalConcurrencyShares`, and borrow limits |\n| `WorkEstimator` (`request/width.go`) | Computes `InitialSeats`, `FinalSeats`, `AdditionalLatency` for each request before `StartRequest` is called |\n| `shufflesharding.Dealer` (`pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go`) | Generates a hand of candidate queue indices from a hash value |\n| `eventclock.Interface` (`fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go`) | Real-time clock and deferred-event scheduling (used for `AdditionalLatency` seat release) |\n\n### Downstream Consumers\n\n| Consumer | What it receives |\n|---|---|\n| `configController.Handle` (`apf_filter.go:155`) | A `fq.Request` handle; calls `Finish(execFn)` to block until dispatched or rejected |\n| Prometheus metrics subsystem | Per-level/schema counters for waiting, executing, dispatched, rejected, seat occupancy, virtual time |\n| Debug endpoint (`/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/...`) | Live `QueueSetDump` snapshots produced by `Dump()` |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Component Responsibilities\n\n### 2.1 `QueueSetFactory` / `queueSetFactory`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:40-45`\n\nA factory that holds a shared `eventclock.Interface` and a `promiseFactoryFactory`. Its sole job is `BeginConstruction`, which validates the `QueuingConfig`, creates a `shufflesharding.Dealer`, and returns a `QueueSetCompleter`. Construction is split into two phases so that validation errors from queuing parameters (phase 1) are surfaced before committing a concurrency allotment (phase 2):\n\n```\nqueueSetFactory.BeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, ...) -> QueueSetCompleter\nQueueSetCompleter.Complete(DispatchingConfig) -> QueueSet\n```\n\nThis two-phase pattern is reused for reconfiguration: `QueueSet.BeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig)` returns a new `QueueSetCompleter` linked to the existing `queueSet`, and `Complete` writes new configuration atomically under the lock.\n\n### 2.2 `queueSet` \u2014 Central State Machine\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:85-167`\n\nThe `queueSet` struct is the heart of the implementation. Key fields (lock-protected unless noted):\n\n| Field | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `queues []*queue` | Slice of per-flow queues; may exceed `DesiredNumQueues` while old queues drain |\n| `currentR SeatSeconds` | Global virtual-time progress meter R (seat-seconds allocated per queue since process start) |\n| `lastRealTime time.Time` | Wall clock at the last virtual-time sync |\n| `robinIndex int` | Round-robin cursor for the dispatch scan |\n| `totSeatsInUse int` | Total seats currently occupied by executing requests |\n| `totSeatsWaiting int` | Sum of `MaxSeats` over all waiting requests |\n| `dealer *shufflesharding.Dealer` | Immutable for the life of a config; replaced on reconfigure |\n| `estimatedServiceDuration` | Fixed at 3ms (line 216); used in virtual-time rate and anti-windup calculations |\n| `promiseFactory` | Produces `WriteOnce` promises for per-request dispatch decisions |\n\nAll methods with suffix `Locked` require the mutex; those without either acquire it or are lock-agnostic.\n\n### 2.3 `queue` \u2014 Per-Flow Queue\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:92-110`\n\nEach `queue` tracks:\n\n- `requestsWaiting fifo` \u2014 a doubly-linked FIFO list (`requestFIFO`, backed by `container/list`) holding waiting `*request` values, plus an aggregated `queueSum` (seat sums and total-work sum maintained incrementally on enqueue/dequeue).\n- `requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]` \u2014 the set of requests from this queue currently in the execution phase.\n- `nextDispatchR SeatSeconds` \u2014 the virtual-time cursor for this queue; the R value at which the next request from this queue will be dispatched in the virtual world. This is the key per-queue state for the SRPT-style fair queuing.\n- `seatsInUse int` \u2014 seats occupied by currently executing requests from this queue (used in virtual-time rate computation).\n\n### 2.4 `request` \u2014 Per-Request Envelope\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:33-83`\n\nWraps one in-flight request. Notable fields:\n\n- `decision promise.WriteOnce` \u2014 a write-once channel-like object. Set to `decisionExecute` by the dispatcher, or set to `decisionCancel` by context cancellation. The goroutine that called `Finish` blocks in `decision.Get()` until one of these happens.\n- `workEstimate completedWorkEstimate` \u2014 holds `InitialSeats`, `FinalSeats`, `AdditionalLatency`, `totalWork` (seat-seconds), and `finalWork`.\n- `arrivalR SeatSeconds` \u2014 value of `currentR` when this request arrived; used by the anti-windup hack.\n- `removeFromQueueLocked removeFromFIFOFunc` \u2014 O(1) closure to remove the request from its queue's FIFO (uses the `list.Element` pointer directly).\n\n### 2.5 `promise.WriteOnce`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/promise/promise.go`, `fairqueuing/promise/interface.go`\n\nA minimal write-once synchronization primitive backed by a channel. `Set` uses `sync.Once` to guarantee idempotence; `Get` blocks on either the set channel or the context's `Done` channel, whichever fires first. When the context fires, `Get` calls `Set(doneVal)` (which is `decisionCancel`) before returning, ensuring `Set` is idempotent even in the cancellation race.\n\nThe key property that makes the locking strategy work: `Set` is always called while holding `qs.lock`, while `Get` is called without the lock (blocking the caller's goroutine independently). This means the dispatcher can write the decision and update queue state atomically, while the waiting goroutine unblocks only after the lock is released.\n\n### 2.6 `requestFIFO`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go`\n\nA `container/list`-backed FIFO with O(1) removal. `Enqueue` returns a closure holding the `*list.Element`; calling it removes the element and updates the `queueSum` aggregate in O(1). `Walk` supports safe concurrent-removal iteration (pre-fetches `current.Next()` before calling `f`).\n\n### 2.7 `shufflesharding.Dealer`\n\n**File:** `pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go`\n\nImplements the shuffle-sharding card-deal algorithm. Given a 64-bit hash and parameters `(deckSize=numQueues, handSize=HandSize)`, it produces a hand of `HandSize` distinct queue indices using Knuth's partial shuffle. The entropy required is `ceil(log2(deckSize) * handSize)` bits, capped at 60 bits of the hash to avoid bias in the last card.\n\n### 2.8 `configController` (APF layer above QueueSet)\n\n**Files:** `apf_controller.go`, `apf_filter.go`\n\nThe `configController` sits above the QueueSet subsystem. It:\n\n- watches `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` API objects via informers, and rebuilds `priorityLevelStates` on any change (`digestConfigObjects`);\n- owns one `priorityLevelState` per priority level, each containing a `fq.QueueSet`;\n- runs a periodic borrowing adjustment loop every 10 seconds (`updateBorrowing`), which reads smoothed seat-demand statistics from each level's `seatDemandIntegrator`, solves an allocation problem (`computeConcurrencyAllocation`), and calls `Complete(DispatchingConfig{ConcurrencyLimit: currentCL})` to push the new limit into the live QueueSet \u2014 without recreating it.\n\n### 2.9 `Integrator`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/integrator.go`\n\nA time-weighted statistical integrator (tracks mean, standard deviation, min, max of a time-series). Each priority level attaches one to its QueueSet's `seatDemandIntegrator` gauge. On each state change (request enters/leaves queue or execution), the QueueSet calls `seatDemandIntegrator.Set(totSeatsInUse + totSeatsWaiting)`. The controller's borrowing loop calls `Reset()` every 10 seconds to harvest statistics and reset the window.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\nThe flow from an incoming HTTP request to execution and completion involves five distinct stages.\n\n### Stage 0: Classification (above QueueSet)\n\nIn `configController.startRequest` (`apf_controller.go:1022`):\n\n1. The `flowSchemas` slice (sorted by matching precedence) is scanned linearly until a `FlowSchema` matches the request's `RequestInfo` and `User`.\n2. The matched FlowSchema identifies a priority level name; the corresponding `priorityLevelState` is looked up.\n3. If the priority level uses queuing (`LimitResponseTypeQueue`) and has more than one queue, a `flowDistinguisher` string is computed (by user name or namespace, per `DistinguisherMethod`) and hashed with the FlowSchema name via SHA-256:\n   ```go\n   // apf_controller.go:1131\n   hash := sha256.New()\n   hash.Write([]byte(fsName)); hash.Write(sep[:]); hash.Write([]byte(fDistinguisher))\n   hashValue = binary.LittleEndian.Uint64(sum[:8])\n   ```\n4. The `WorkEstimator` is called to produce `InitialSeats`, `FinalSeats`, `AdditionalLatency`.\n5. `plState.queues.StartRequest(ctx, &workEstimate, hashValue, ...)` is called \u2014 entering the QueueSet.\n\n### Stage 1: `StartRequest` \u2014 Queue Assignment and Enqueue\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:308`\n\nUnder the QueueSet's mutex (acquired via `lockAndSyncTime` which also advances virtual time):\n\n**Path A \u2014 no queuing** (`DesiredNumQueues < 1`):\n\n`canAccommodateSeatsLocked` checks `totSeatsInUse + request.MaxSeats() <= ConcurrencyLimit`. If it fails, the request is rejected immediately with reason `\"concurrency-limit\"` and `nil` is returned. If it passes, `dispatchSansQueueLocked` is called, which creates the request with `decision` pre-set to `decisionExecute`, increments executing counters, and returns immediately.\n\n**Path B \u2014 with queuing** (`DesiredNumQueues >= 1`):\n\n1. **Shuffle-sharding** (`shuffleShardLocked`, line 583): The dealer deals `HandSize` cards (queue indices) from the hash. The QueueSet iterates the hand starting at a rotating offset (`qs.enqueues % handSize`) to remove ordering bias, picks the queue with the minimum `TotalWorkSum` (total seat-seconds of waiting work), and selects it as the target.\n\n2. **Reject or enqueue** (`rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked`, line 618): Rejection fires only if *both* conditions hold simultaneously:\n   ```\n   totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit  AND  queue.requestsWaiting.Length() >= QueueLengthLimit\n   ```\n   If either condition is not met, the request is enqueued in the selected queue's FIFO. The `arrivalR` is set to `currentR` at enqueue time; if the queue was idle, `nextDispatchR` is also reset to `currentR` (avoiding an empty queue inheriting a stale virtual start).\n\n3. **Dispatch loop** (`dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked`, line 654): After enqueue, this loop fires and may immediately dispatch the newly enqueued request or other waiting requests:\n   ```go\n   for qs.totRequestsWaiting != 0 && qs.totSeatsInUse < qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit && qs.dispatchLocked() {\n   }\n   ```\n\n### Stage 2: Dispatch Selection (`dispatchLocked` / `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`)\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:695-843`\n\nThe dispatcher selects the best queue to dispatch from using a **virtual-finish-time** criterion, equivalent to Shortest Remaining Processing Time across queues:\n\n```\nvirtualFinish(queue) = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()\n```\n\nThe scan iterates all queues in round-robin order (resuming from `robinIndex`) and finds the queue with the minimum `virtualFinish`. This biases toward queues that have been waiting longest in virtual time, achieving fairness across flows.\n\nAfter selecting the queue:\n\n- `canAccommodateSeatsLocked` is called for the head request. If `request.MaxSeats() > ConcurrencyLimit` and there are currently executing requests, dispatch stalls \u2014 the loop exits and will retry when a request finishes.\n- The head request is dequeued (O(1) via its `removeFromQueueLocked` closure).\n- `FinalSeats` are clamped to `ConcurrencyLimit` if they would exceed it, with `AdditionalLatency` adjusted to preserve total work.\n- **Virtual time is advanced**: `queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()` (seat-seconds consumed in the virtual world). This is the core progress accounting: a queue that dispatches more work accumulates a higher `nextDispatchR`, naturally reducing its priority for subsequent dispatches.\n- `request.decision.Set(decisionExecute)` is called under the lock, unblocking the waiting goroutine.\n\n### Stage 3: Waiting (`request.wait`)\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:397`\n\nThe goroutine that called `StartRequest` (and received a non-nil `Request`) calls `req.Finish(execFn)`, which internally calls `req.wait()`:\n\n```go\ndecisionAny := req.decision.Get()  // blocks here until dispatched or cancelled\n```\n\n`Get` blocks on `select { case <-p.setCh: ... case <-p.doneCtx.Done(): ... }`. If the context fires first, `Set(decisionCancel)` races with the dispatcher's `Set(decisionExecute)` \u2014 only one wins (via `sync.Once`). After returning from `Get`, `wait` acquires the lock to finalize state:\n\n- `decisionExecute`: return `(true, false)` \u2014 proceed to execution.\n- `decisionCancel`: if the request is still in its queue (i.e., `removeFromQueueLocked()` returns non-nil), it is removed, counters are decremented, and reason `\"time-out\"` is recorded in metrics.\n\n### Stage 4: Execution and Seat Release (`finishRequestLocked`)\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:863`\n\nAfter `execFn()` returns, `finishRequestLocked` is called:\n\n1. The request is removed from `queue.requestsExecuting`.\n2. **Virtual-time correction**: The queue's `nextDispatchR` is adjusted for the difference between estimated and actual service time:\n   ```go\n   queue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(float64(r.InitialSeats()), estimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration)\n   ```\n   This retroactively corrects the virtual-time ledger: if actual service was shorter than the 3ms estimate, `nextDispatchR` is wound back, giving this queue's next request an earlier virtual start than it would otherwise have had.\n3. `boundNextDispatchLocked` (the anti-windup hack) is then applied: if `nextDispatchR` fell below the oldest waiting request's `arrivalR`, it is clamped up to `arrivalR`. This prevents a queue from accumulating an unfairly early virtual start when it is lightly loaded.\n4. **Seat release \u2014 immediate or deferred**: If `AdditionalLatency <= 0`, seats are released immediately. Otherwise, `qs.clock.EventAfterDuration(releaseSeatsLocked, additionalLatency)` schedules seat release in a new goroutine after the additional latency. This models requests (e.g., watches) that hold server resources beyond their initial response.\n5. `removeQueueIfEmptyLocked` removes queues that are both empty and in excess of `DesiredNumQueues` (queue shrinkage by attrition).\n6. `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` is called to dispatch any newly eligible requests.\n\n---\n\n## 4. The Fair Queuing Algorithm in Detail\n\n### Virtual Time (`currentR`)\n\n`currentR` is a global seat-seconds counter, advanced in `syncTimeLocked` every time the lock is acquired:\n\n```go\n// queueset.go:470\nincrR = SeatsTimesDuration(getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\nqs.currentR = prevR + incrR\n```\n\nThe **virtual time ratio** (`getVirtualTimeRatioLocked`, line 526) is:\n\n```\nratio = min(sum(seatsRequested across active queues), ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n```\n\nwhere `seatsRequested` for a queue is `seatsInUse + MaxSeatsSum(waiting)`. This models each active queue as receiving an equal share of the concurrency budget \u2014 the foundation of the fairness guarantee.\n\nWhen no queues are active, the ratio is 0 and virtual time freezes (no work is being done).\n\n### Queue Selection for Dispatch\n\nThe dispatcher selects the queue minimizing:\n\n```\nnextDispatchR + totalWork(head request)\n```\n\n`nextDispatchR` reflects how much virtual-time work this queue has already been allocated. Adding the head request's work gives the virtual finish time of the next item if dispatched from this queue. Choosing the minimum ensures the queue that has received the least service (in virtual time) gets priority \u2014 weighted by request size.\n\n### Work Units: `SeatSeconds`\n\n**File:** `request/seat_seconds.go`\n\n`SeatSeconds` is a fixed-point `uint64` with scale factor `1e8` (i.e., 1 seat-second = `1e8` units). This avoids floating-point arithmetic in the hot path while providing nanosecond-scale granularity for the 3ms estimated service duration.\n\n`totalWork` for a request is:\n\n```\ntotalWork = SeatsTimesDuration(InitialSeats, estimatedServiceDuration) + SeatsTimesDuration(FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency)\n```\n\nThis means a request that uses more seats or has additional latency consumes proportionally more virtual-time budget, correctly penalizing heavy requests.\n\n### Epoch Advancement (Overflow Prevention)\n\n**File:** `queueset.go:489-522`\n\n`currentR` and all `nextDispatchR` / `arrivalR` values are `uint64`. To prevent overflow, when `currentR >= highR` (approximately 3/4 of `MaxSeatSeconds`), `advanceEpoch` subtracts `rDecrement = MaxSeatSeconds/2` from `currentR` and all per-queue and per-request readings. Idle queues have their `nextDispatchR` reset to 0 (safe because their value is stale). Overflow in the subtraction (underflow of unsigned values) is detected and logged.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 5.1 Queue Full Rejection\n\nA request is rejected with `\"queue-full\"` if and only if the selected queue is full **and** the QueueSet is at its concurrency limit simultaneously (`rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked`, line 618). The \"and\" is deliberate: if seats are available, requests are still accepted even if queues are deep, since they can be dispatched immediately. This avoids spurious rejection under bursty load.\n\n**Operational risk**: Misconfigured `QueueLengthLimit` (too low) causes premature rejection under legitimate load spikes. Too high wastes memory and allows unbounded latency accumulation.\n\n### 5.2 Oversized Requests\n\nIf `request.MaxSeats() > ConcurrencyLimit` and other requests are executing, the request cannot be dispatched \u2014 `canAccommodateSeatsLocked` returns false and the dispatch loop stalls. The request waits in its queue. If the request is the *only* thing in the system (`totRequestsExecuting == 0`), it is allowed through anyway to avoid starvation.\n\n**Tradeoff**: This prevents seat arithmetic overflow, but a single oversized request can temporarily block an entire QueueSet.\n\n### 5.3 Virtual Time Windup (Anti-Windup Hack)\n\nA queue that receives no requests for a long time has a stale `nextDispatchR` (from its last dispatch). When it later receives a request, `nextDispatchR` could be far in the past relative to `currentR`, making this queue appear to be owed an enormous amount of service. The anti-windup `boundNextDispatchLocked` (line 952) clamps `nextDispatchR` upward to `oldestWaiting.arrivalR`:\n\n```go\nif queue.nextDispatchR < virtualStartBound {\n    queue.nextDispatchR = virtualStartBound\n}\n```\n\n**Tradeoff**: This is a pragmatic approximation. It prevents windfall service for bursty flows but means a flow that goes idle and returns cannot \"bank\" its unused capacity \u2014 each flow gets at most its fair share going forward.\n\n### 5.4 `estimatedServiceDuration` Is a Fixed Constant\n\n`estimatedServiceDuration` is hardcoded at 3ms (`queueset.go:216`). This estimate is used in:\n\n- Computing `totalWork` for virtual-time bookkeeping (the initial-phase component).\n- Computing `estimatedWorkInProgress` in `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked` (for the `dsMin`/`dsMax` metrics).\n- Post-execution `nextDispatchR` correction: if actual service took 10ms instead of 3ms, `nextDispatchR` is reduced by `7ms * InitialSeats`.\n\n**Risk**: If actual request service times are systematically far from 3ms (e.g., long-running list requests), the virtual-time accounting during queuing is inaccurate. The post-execution correction partially compensates but applies only retroactively.\n\n### 5.5 Borrowing and the `ConcurrencyLimit` Race\n\nThe `ConcurrencyLimit` for a QueueSet is updated every 10 seconds by the borrowing loop via `Complete(DispatchingConfig{ConcurrencyLimit: currentCL})`. `Complete` calls `setConfiguration`, which calls `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` \u2014 meaning the new limit takes effect immediately for dispatch decisions. Between adjustment periods, a priority level with a temporarily lower limit may queue requests that would have been admitted under the old limit.\n\n**Tradeoff**: The 10-second borrowing period provides smoothing (via `seatDemandSmoothingCoefficient = 0.977`, half-life ~5 minutes) against transient load spikes, at the cost of slow adaptation. A sudden traffic surge takes minutes to fully propagate to increased concurrency for a needy level.\n\n### 5.6 `AdditionalLatency` and Deferred Seat Release\n\nWatch requests and large list responses that hold server-side resources after the response headers are sent are modeled with `FinalSeats` and `AdditionalLatency`. The `EventAfterDuration` mechanism schedules seat release asynchronously, so the response is delivered to the client while APF continues to account for the held seats. This correctly models resource consumption but adds complexity:\n\n- A goroutine is spawned per request with non-zero `AdditionalLatency`.\n- Seat release may race with QueueSet reconfiguration.\n- Metrics (`execSeatsGauge`) remain elevated during the additional latency, which is correct but may surprise operators reading dashboards.\n\n### 5.7 Lock Contention\n\nThe entire `queueSet` is protected by a single `sync.Mutex`. Every call to `StartRequest`, `Finish`, and the `EventAfterDuration` callback acquires this lock. Under high request rates this becomes a serialization point. The `syncTimeLocked` call at every lock acquisition advances virtual time \u2014 adding a small but constant overhead proportional to time elapsed.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 6.1 `QueueSetFactory` Interface\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/interface.go:32`\n\nProduction code uses `fqs.NewQueueSetFactory(clk)` (`apf_filter.go:105`). Tests may substitute a `newTestableQueueSetFactory` with a different `promiseFactoryFactory`. The interface is fully replaceable, but in practice the only real implementation is `queueSetFactory` in the `queueset` package.\n\n**Risk**: Replacing the factory is not a supported operator configuration; it requires Go-level code changes.\n\n### 6.2 `promiseFactoryFactory` \u2014 Testability Hook\n\n**File:** `queueset.go:47-54`\n\nThe `promiseFactoryFactory` is a function that, given a `*queueSet`, returns a factory for `WriteOnce` promises. The production factory returns `promise.NewWriteOnce`. Test code can substitute a fake that allows deterministic control of when dispatch decisions are delivered.\n\nThis hook exists purely to make the dispatch-wait race testable without real goroutines and wall-clock time.\n\n### 6.3 `eventclock.Interface` \u2014 Clock Abstraction\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go`\n\nAll time-based operations go through `eventclock.Interface` (which embeds `clock.PassiveClock`). Tests supply a `FakeClock` that controls time and deferred events manually. The real implementation (`eventclock.Real`) wraps standard Go time functions.\n\n**Extension risk**: The clock is wired at `New()` time (`apf_filter.go:94`, `Real{}`). Operators cannot substitute a custom clock without modifying the source.\n\n### 6.4 `WorkEstimator` \u2014 Pluggable Request Sizing\n\n**File:** `request/width.go:75`\n\n`NewWorkEstimator` takes four parameters:\n\n- `objectCountFn` \u2014 returns the stored object count for a resource (used by the list estimator).\n- `watchCountFn` \u2014 returns the number of interested watchers for a request (used by the mutating estimator, which accounts for watch fan-out).\n- `config *WorkEstimatorConfig` \u2014 minimum/maximum seat limits.\n- `maxSeatsFn` \u2014 returns the per-priority-level maximum seats (tracked by `MaxSeatsTracker`, set at 15% of `nominalCL`, `apf_controller.go:63`).\n\nOperators can influence work estimation indirectly through `PriorityLevelConfiguration.spec.limited.limitResponse.queuing` fields and by the object count and watch count functions, which are populated from storage backends.\n\n**Risk**: The work estimator is called while holding `cfgCtlr.lock.RLock()` (inside `startRequest`). A slow `objectCountFn` or `watchCountFn` would hold the read lock and stall all concurrent classification.\n\n### 6.5 `FlowDistinguisherMethod` \u2014 Flow Partitioning\n\n**File:** `apf_controller.go:1115-1129`\n\nThe `flowDistinguisher` fed into hash computation is determined by `DistinguisherMethod.Type`:\n\n- `ByUser` \u2014 uses `rd.User.GetName()`\n- `ByNamespace` \u2014 uses `rd.RequestInfo.Namespace`\n\nThis is the only operator-controlled knob that affects which queue within a priority level a given request lands in. It is set per FlowSchema in the API object. A single-queue priority level ignores it entirely (no shuffle-sharding).\n\n**Tradeoff**: `ByUser` provides isolation between users of the same priority level; `ByNamespace` provides isolation between namespaces. Neither provides isolation across multiple dimensions simultaneously.\n\n### 6.6 `QueueSet.Dump` \u2014 Debug Introspection\n\n**File:** `queueset.go:996`\n\n`Dump(includeRequestDetails bool)` acquires the lock, snapshots all queue state, and returns a `debug.QueueSetDump`. With `includeRequestDetails=true` it also extracts `UserInfo` and `RequestInfo` from the request contexts. This is exposed via the APF debug HTTP endpoint installed by `Install(mux)`.\n\n**Risk**: `Dump` holds the QueueSet lock for the duration of the snapshot. On a large, busy QueueSet this can cause momentary stalls to all concurrent requests.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications\n\n### 7.1 Diagnosing Rejections\n\nThree rejection reasons appear in `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total`:\n\n| Reason | Source | Meaning |\n|---|---|---|\n| `concurrency-limit` | `StartRequest` path A | No-queue priority level hit its seat limit |\n| `queue-full` | `StartRequest` path B | Both queue-length and seat-limit exceeded simultaneously |\n| `time-out` | `request.wait` | Request context cancelled while waiting |\n\n`queue-full` rejections are the primary signal of overload at a priority level. `time-out` rejections indicate clients with short deadlines experiencing sustained queue depth. Neither is necessarily pathological \u2014 some rejection is expected and healthy under overload \u2014 but sustained high rates warrant attention.\n\n### 7.2 Monitoring Virtual Time\n\n`apiserver_flowcontrol_current_r` (set via `metrics.SetCurrentR`) tracks `currentR` per priority level. A monotonically advancing `currentR` indicates the priority level is active. A `currentR` that advances very slowly relative to other levels indicates few active queues or low seat demand.\n\n`apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatch_r`, `apiserver_flowcontrol_latest_s`, and related metrics (set via `metrics.SetDispatchMetrics`) expose `minVirtualFinish`, `sMin`, `sMax`, `dsMin`, `dsMax` from `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`. These are useful for understanding the spread of virtual times across queues \u2014 a large `sMax - sMin` indicates significant imbalance in how much service different flows have received.\n\n### 7.3 Seat Demand and Borrowing Observability\n\n`apiserver_flowcontrol_priority_level_seat_count_samples` tracks the time-weighted integral of seat demand per priority level. The borrowing loop reads this every 10 seconds and adjusts `currentCL`. `apiserver_flowcontrol_lower_limit_seats`, `apiserver_flowcontrol_upper_limit_seats`, and `apiserver_flowcontrol_nominal_limit_seats` expose the bounds within which `currentCL` can move.\n\nIf a priority level is consistently borrowing (its `currentCL` is above its `nominalCL`), other levels are lending it capacity \u2014 verify that the lenders are not starved.\n\n### 7.4 The 3ms Estimation Problem in Practice\n\nBecause `estimatedServiceDuration = 3ms` is fixed, list requests that complete in 500ms inflate a queue's `nextDispatchR` by only `InitialSeats * 3ms` during queuing. The post-execution correction applies after the fact. This means:\n\n- During a queue backup, the virtual-time selection algorithm underestimates the true cost of list requests.\n- Queues containing large lists may be over-dispatched before the correction kicks in.\n- The `WorkEstimate.FinalSeats + AdditionalLatency` portion is accounted correctly in virtual time, since `AdditionalLatency` is a real measured quantity computed by the work estimator from watch fan-out.\n\n### 7.5 Configuration Stability Concerns\n\nEvery change to any `FlowSchema` or `PriorityLevelConfiguration` object triggers a full re-digest of all config objects (`lockAndDigestConfigObjects`). During this re-digest, `cfgCtlr.lock` is held in write mode, blocking all concurrent `startRequest` calls (which need the read lock). This is bounded by informer event rate but can cause brief stalls under heavy automated config churn (e.g., frequent operator or controller writes).\n\nWhen `DesiredNumQueues` decreases, excess queues are not discarded immediately \u2014 they drain by attrition (`removeQueueIfEmptyLocked`). During draining, the queue count exceeds `DesiredNumQueues`, which means shuffle-sharding deals from more queues than configured, slightly reducing isolation guarantees until all excess queues are empty.\n\n### 7.6 Memory Budget\n\nEach `queue` holds a `requestFIFO` of waiting `*request` values plus a `sets.Set[*request]` of executing ones. With `N` priority levels each having `Q` queues and `L` max queue length, the worst-case waiting-request memory is `N * Q * L * sizeof(request)`. A `request` struct carries its context, work estimate, and two `interface{}` descriptors \u2014 roughly 200\u2013400 bytes depending on context size. For typical APF configs (e.g., 64 queues, 50-item limit), this is negligible, but operators who configure very large queue depths should account for memory usage under pathological overload.\n\n---\n\n## 8. File Map\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_filter.go                    Interface definition, Handle() entry point,\n\u2502 {
  "content": "# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries](#1-subsystem-purpose-and-boundaries)\n2. [Component Responsibilities](#2-component-responsibilities)\n3. [End-to-End Request Flow](#3-end-to-end-request-flow)\n4. [The Fair Queuing Algorithm in Detail](#4-the-fair-queuing-algorithm-in-detail)\n5. [Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs](#5-failure-modes-limits-and-design-tradeoffs)\n6. [Extension Points and Customization Hooks](#6-extension-points-and-customization-hooks)\n7. [Operational Implications](#7-operational-implications)\n8. [File Map](#8-file-map)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe APF (API Priority and Fairness) QueueSet subsystem implements **Fair Queuing for Server Requests** inside the Kubernetes API server. Its job is to prevent any single client or flow from monopolizing the apiserver's concurrency budget, while still making forward progress for all active flows under overload.\n\nEvery non-exempt apiserver request is routed through a *priority level*, each of which owns exactly one `QueueSet`. The `QueueSet` for a priority level is the gate that decides:\n\n- whether an incoming request can be dispatched immediately (seats available),\n- whether it must wait in a queue (backpressure),\n- whether it must be rejected outright (queue full and concurrency limit exceeded), or\n- whether it times out while waiting (context cancelled).\n\n### Scope Boundary\n\nThe QueueSet subsystem is responsible only for **queuing and dispatch decisions** within a single priority level. It has no knowledge of:\n\n- how requests are classified (FlowSchema matching happens in `apf_controller.go`);\n- cross-level concurrency borrowing (also handled at the controller layer);\n- HTTP-level admission or request routing.\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\n| Dependency | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `configController` (`apf_controller.go`) | Creates and reconfigures QueueSets; provides `ConcurrencyLimit` and queuing parameters |\n| `FlowSchema` / `PriorityLevelConfiguration` API objects | Supply `HandSize`, `Queues`, `QueueLengthLimit`, `NominalConcurrencyShares`, and borrow limits |\n| `WorkEstimator` (`request/width.go`) | Computes `InitialSeats`, `FinalSeats`, `AdditionalLatency` for each request before `StartRequest` is called |\n| `shufflesharding.Dealer` (`pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go`) | Generates a hand of candidate queue indices from a hash value |\n| `eventclock.Interface` (`fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go`) | Real-time clock and deferred-event scheduling (used for `AdditionalLatency` seat release) |\n\n### Downstream Consumers\n\n| Consumer | What it receives |\n|---|---|\n| `configController.Handle` (`apf_filter.go:155`) | A `fq.Request` handle; calls `Finish(execFn)` to block until dispatched or rejected |\n| Prometheus metrics subsystem | Per-level/schema counters for waiting, executing, dispatched, rejected, seat occupancy, virtual time |\n| Debug endpoint (`/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/...`) | Live `QueueSetDump` snapshots produced by `Dump()` |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Component Responsibilities\n\n### 2.1 `QueueSetFactory` / `queueSetFactory`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:40-45`\n\nA factory that holds a shared `eventclock.Interface` and a `promiseFactoryFactory`. Its sole job is `BeginConstruction`, which validates the `QueuingConfig`, creates a `shufflesharding.Dealer`, and returns a `QueueSetCompleter`. Construction is split into two phases so that validation errors from queuing parameters (phase 1) are surfaced before committing a concurrency allotment (phase 2):\n\n```\nqueueSetFactory.BeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, ...) -> QueueSetCompleter\nQueueSetCompleter.Complete(DispatchingConfig) -> QueueSet\n```\n\nThis two-phase pattern is reused for reconfiguration: `QueueSet.BeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig)` returns a new `QueueSetCompleter` linked to the existing `queueSet`, and `Complete` writes new configuration atomically under the lock.\n\n### 2.2 `queueSet` \u2014 Central State Machine\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:85-167`\n\nThe `queueSet` struct is the heart of the implementation. Key fields (lock-protected unless noted):\n\n| Field | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `queues []*queue` | Slice of per-flow queues; may exceed `DesiredNumQueues` while old queues drain |\n| `currentR SeatSeconds` | Global virtual-time progress meter R (seat-seconds allocated per queue since process start) |\n| `lastRealTime time.Time` | Wall clock at the last virtual-time sync |\n| `robinIndex int` | Round-robin cursor for the dispatch scan |\n| `totSeatsInUse int` | Total seats currently occupied by executing requests |\n| `totSeatsWaiting int` | Sum of `MaxSeats` over all waiting requests |\n| `dealer *shufflesharding.Dealer` | Immutable for the life of a config; replaced on reconfigure |\n| `estimatedServiceDuration` | Fixed at 3ms (line 216); used in virtual-time rate and anti-windup calculations |\n| `promiseFactory` | Produces `WriteOnce` promises for per-request dispatch decisions |\n\nAll methods with suffix `Locked` require the mutex; those without either acquire it or are lock-agnostic.\n\n### 2.3 `queue` \u2014 Per-Flow Queue\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:92-110`\n\nEach `queue` tracks:\n\n- `requestsWaiting fifo` \u2014 a doubly-linked FIFO list (`requestFIFO`, backed by `container/list`) holding waiting `*request` values, plus an aggregated `queueSum` (seat sums and total-work sum maintained incrementally on enqueue/dequeue).\n- `requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]` \u2014 the set of requests from this queue currently in the execution phase.\n- `nextDispatchR SeatSeconds` \u2014 the virtual-time cursor for this queue; the R value at which the next request from this queue will be dispatched in the virtual world. This is the key per-queue state for the SRPT-style fair queuing.\n- `seatsInUse int` \u2014 seats occupied by currently executing requests from this queue (used in virtual-time rate computation).\n\n### 2.4 `request` \u2014 Per-Request Envelope\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:33-83`\n\nWraps one in-flight request. Notable fields:\n\n- `decision promise.WriteOnce` \u2014 a write-once channel-like object. Set to `decisionExecute` by the dispatcher, or set to `decisionCancel` by context cancellation. The goroutine that called `Finish` blocks in `decision.Get()` until one of these happens.\n- `workEstimate completedWorkEstimate` \u2014 holds `InitialSeats`, `FinalSeats`, `AdditionalLatency`, `totalWork` (seat-seconds), and `finalWork`.\n- `arrivalR SeatSeconds` \u2014 value of `currentR` when this request arrived; used by the anti-windup hack.\n- `removeFromQueueLocked removeFromFIFOFunc` \u2014 O(1) closure to remove the request from its queue's FIFO (uses the `list.Element` pointer directly).\n\n### 2.5 `promise.WriteOnce`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/promise/promise.go`, `fairqueuing/promise/interface.go`\n\nA minimal write-once synchronization primitive backed by a channel. `Set` uses `sync.Once` to guarantee idempotence; `Get` blocks on either the set channel or the context's `Done` channel, whichever fires first. When the context fires, `Get` calls `Set(doneVal)` (which is `decisionCancel`) before returning, ensuring `Set` is idempotent even in the cancellation race.\n\nThe key property that makes the locking strategy work: `Set` is always called while holding `qs.lock`, while `Get` is called without the lock (blocking the caller's goroutine independently). This means the dispatcher can write the decision and update queue state atomically, while the waiting goroutine unblocks only after the lock is released.\n\n### 2.6 `requestFIFO`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go`\n\nA `container/list`-backed FIFO with O(1) removal. `Enqueue` returns a closure holding the `*list.Element`; calling it removes the element and updates the `queueSum` aggregate in O(1). `Walk` supports safe concurrent-removal iteration (pre-fetches `current.Next()` before calling `f`).\n\n### 2.7 `shufflesharding.Dealer`\n\n**File:** `pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go`\n\nImplements the shuffle-sharding card-deal algorithm. Given a 64-bit hash and parameters `(deckSize=numQueues, handSize=HandSize)`, it produces a hand of `HandSize` distinct queue indices using Knuth's partial shuffle. The entropy required is `ceil(log2(deckSize) * handSize)` bits, capped at 60 bits of the hash to avoid bias in the last card.\n\n### 2.8 `configController` (APF layer above QueueSet)\n\n**Files:** `apf_controller.go`, `apf_filter.go`\n\nThe `configController` sits above the QueueSet subsystem. It:\n\n- watches `FlowSchema` and `PriorityLevelConfiguration` API objects via informers, and rebuilds `priorityLevelStates` on any change (`digestConfigObjects`);\n- owns one `priorityLevelState` per priority level, each containing a `fq.QueueSet`;\n- runs a periodic borrowing adjustment loop every 10 seconds (`updateBorrowing`), which reads smoothed seat-demand statistics from each level's `seatDemandIntegrator`, solves an allocation problem (`computeConcurrencyAllocation`), and calls `Complete(DispatchingConfig{ConcurrencyLimit: currentCL})` to push the new limit into the live QueueSet \u2014 without recreating it.\n\n### 2.9 `Integrator`\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/integrator.go`\n\nA time-weighted statistical integrator (tracks mean, standard deviation, min, max of a time-series). Each priority level attaches one to its QueueSet's `seatDemandIntegrator` gauge. On each state change (request enters/leaves queue or execution), the QueueSet calls `seatDemandIntegrator.Set(totSeatsInUse + totSeatsWaiting)`. The controller's borrowing loop calls `Reset()` every 10 seconds to harvest statistics and reset the window.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\nThe flow from an incoming HTTP request to execution and completion involves five distinct stages.\n\n### Stage 0: Classification (above QueueSet)\n\nIn `configController.startRequest` (`apf_controller.go:1022`):\n\n1. The `flowSchemas` slice (sorted by matching precedence) is scanned linearly until a `FlowSchema` matches the request's `RequestInfo` and `User`.\n2. The matched FlowSchema identifies a priority level name; the corresponding `priorityLevelState` is looked up.\n3. If the priority level uses queuing (`LimitResponseTypeQueue`) and has more than one queue, a `flowDistinguisher` string is computed (by user name or namespace, per `DistinguisherMethod`) and hashed with the FlowSchema name via SHA-256:\n   ```go\n   // apf_controller.go:1131\n   hash := sha256.New()\n   hash.Write([]byte(fsName)); hash.Write(sep[:]); hash.Write([]byte(fDistinguisher))\n   hashValue = binary.LittleEndian.Uint64(sum[:8])\n   ```\n4. The `WorkEstimator` is called to produce `InitialSeats`, `FinalSeats`, `AdditionalLatency`.\n5. `plState.queues.StartRequest(ctx, &workEstimate, hashValue, ...)` is called \u2014 entering the QueueSet.\n\n### Stage 1: `StartRequest` \u2014 Queue Assignment and Enqueue\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:308`\n\nUnder the QueueSet's mutex (acquired via `lockAndSyncTime` which also advances virtual time):\n\n**Path A \u2014 no queuing** (`DesiredNumQueues < 1`):\n\n`canAccommodateSeatsLocked` checks `totSeatsInUse + request.MaxSeats() <= ConcurrencyLimit`. If it fails, the request is rejected immediately with reason `\"concurrency-limit\"` and `nil` is returned. If it passes, `dispatchSansQueueLocked` is called, which creates the request with `decision` pre-set to `decisionExecute`, increments executing counters, and returns immediately.\n\n**Path B \u2014 with queuing** (`DesiredNumQueues >= 1`):\n\n1. **Shuffle-sharding** (`shuffleShardLocked`, line 583): The dealer deals `HandSize` cards (queue indices) from the hash. The QueueSet iterates the hand starting at a rotating offset (`qs.enqueues % handSize`) to remove ordering bias, picks the queue with the minimum `TotalWorkSum` (total seat-seconds of waiting work), and selects it as the target.\n\n2. **Reject or enqueue** (`rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked`, line 618): Rejection fires only if *both* conditions hold simultaneously:\n   ```\n   totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit  AND  queue.requestsWaiting.Length() >= QueueLengthLimit\n   ```\n   If either condition is not met, the request is enqueued in the selected queue's FIFO. The `arrivalR` is set to `currentR` at enqueue time; if the queue was idle, `nextDispatchR` is also reset to `currentR` (avoiding an empty queue inheriting a stale virtual start).\n\n3. **Dispatch loop** (`dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked`, line 654): After enqueue, this loop fires and may immediately dispatch the newly enqueued request or other waiting requests:\n   ```go\n   for qs.totRequestsWaiting != 0 && qs.totSeatsInUse < qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit && qs.dispatchLocked() {\n   }\n   ```\n\n### Stage 2: Dispatch Selection (`dispatchLocked` / `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`)\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:695-843`\n\nThe dispatcher selects the best queue to dispatch from using a **virtual-finish-time** criterion, equivalent to Shortest Remaining Processing Time across queues:\n\n```\nvirtualFinish(queue) = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()\n```\n\nThe scan iterates all queues in round-robin order (resuming from `robinIndex`) and finds the queue with the minimum `virtualFinish`. This biases toward queues that have been waiting longest in virtual time, achieving fairness across flows.\n\nAfter selecting the queue:\n\n- `canAccommodateSeatsLocked` is called for the head request. If `request.MaxSeats() > ConcurrencyLimit` and there are currently executing requests, dispatch stalls \u2014 the loop exits and will retry when a request finishes.\n- The head request is dequeued (O(1) via its `removeFromQueueLocked` closure).\n- `FinalSeats` are clamped to `ConcurrencyLimit` if they would exceed it, with `AdditionalLatency` adjusted to preserve total work.\n- **Virtual time is advanced**: `queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()` (seat-seconds consumed in the virtual world). This is the core progress accounting: a queue that dispatches more work accumulates a higher `nextDispatchR`, naturally reducing its priority for subsequent dispatches.\n- `request.decision.Set(decisionExecute)` is called under the lock, unblocking the waiting goroutine.\n\n### Stage 3: Waiting (`request.wait`)\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:397`\n\nThe goroutine that called `StartRequest` (and received a non-nil `Request`) calls `req.Finish(execFn)`, which internally calls `req.wait()`:\n\n```go\ndecisionAny := req.decision.Get()  // blocks here until dispatched or cancelled\n```\n\n`Get` blocks on `select { case <-p.setCh: ... case <-p.doneCtx.Done(): ... }`. If the context fires first, `Set(decisionCancel)` races with the dispatcher's `Set(decisionExecute)` \u2014 only one wins (via `sync.Once`). After returning from `Get`, `wait` acquires the lock to finalize state:\n\n- `decisionExecute`: return `(true, false)` \u2014 proceed to execution.\n- `decisionCancel`: if the request is still in its queue (i.e., `removeFromQueueLocked()` returns non-nil), it is removed, counters are decremented, and reason `\"time-out\"` is recorded in metrics.\n\n### Stage 4: Execution and Seat Release (`finishRequestLocked`)\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go:863`\n\nAfter `execFn()` returns, `finishRequestLocked` is called:\n\n1. The request is removed from `queue.requestsExecuting`.\n2. **Virtual-time correction**: The queue's `nextDispatchR` is adjusted for the difference between estimated and actual service time:\n   ```go\n   queue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(float64(r.InitialSeats()), estimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration)\n   ```\n   This retroactively corrects the virtual-time ledger: if actual service was shorter than the 3ms estimate, `nextDispatchR` is wound back, giving this queue's next request an earlier virtual start than it would otherwise have had.\n3. `boundNextDispatchLocked` (the anti-windup hack) is then applied: if `nextDispatchR` fell below the oldest waiting request's `arrivalR`, it is clamped up to `arrivalR`. This prevents a queue from accumulating an unfairly early virtual start when it is lightly loaded.\n4. **Seat release \u2014 immediate or deferred**: If `AdditionalLatency <= 0`, seats are released immediately. Otherwise, `qs.clock.EventAfterDuration(releaseSeatsLocked, additionalLatency)` schedules seat release in a new goroutine after the additional latency. This models requests (e.g., watches) that hold server resources beyond their initial response.\n5. `removeQueueIfEmptyLocked` removes queues that are both empty and in excess of `DesiredNumQueues` (queue shrinkage by attrition).\n6. `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` is called to dispatch any newly eligible requests.\n\n---\n\n## 4. The Fair Queuing Algorithm in Detail\n\n### Virtual Time (`currentR`)\n\n`currentR` is a global seat-seconds counter, advanced in `syncTimeLocked` every time the lock is acquired:\n\n```go\n// queueset.go:470\nincrR = SeatsTimesDuration(getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\nqs.currentR = prevR + incrR\n```\n\nThe **virtual time ratio** (`getVirtualTimeRatioLocked`, line 526) is:\n\n```\nratio = min(sum(seatsRequested across active queues), ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n```\n\nwhere `seatsRequested` for a queue is `seatsInUse + MaxSeatsSum(waiting)`. This models each active queue as receiving an equal share of the concurrency budget \u2014 the foundation of the fairness guarantee.\n\nWhen no queues are active, the ratio is 0 and virtual time freezes (no work is being done).\n\n### Queue Selection for Dispatch\n\nThe dispatcher selects the queue minimizing:\n\n```\nnextDispatchR + totalWork(head request)\n```\n\n`nextDispatchR` reflects how much virtual-time work this queue has already been allocated. Adding the head request's work gives the virtual finish time of the next item if dispatched from this queue. Choosing the minimum ensures the queue that has received the least service (in virtual time) gets priority \u2014 weighted by request size.\n\n### Work Units: `SeatSeconds`\n\n**File:** `request/seat_seconds.go`\n\n`SeatSeconds` is a fixed-point `uint64` with scale factor `1e8` (i.e., 1 seat-second = `1e8` units). This avoids floating-point arithmetic in the hot path while providing nanosecond-scale granularity for the 3ms estimated service duration.\n\n`totalWork` for a request is:\n\n```\ntotalWork = SeatsTimesDuration(InitialSeats, estimatedServiceDuration) + SeatsTimesDuration(FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency)\n```\n\nThis means a request that uses more seats or has additional latency consumes proportionally more virtual-time budget, correctly penalizing heavy requests.\n\n### Epoch Advancement (Overflow Prevention)\n\n**File:** `queueset.go:489-522`\n\n`currentR` and all `nextDispatchR` / `arrivalR` values are `uint64`. To prevent overflow, when `currentR >= highR` (approximately 3/4 of `MaxSeatSeconds`), `advanceEpoch` subtracts `rDecrement = MaxSeatSeconds/2` from `currentR` and all per-queue and per-request readings. Idle queues have their `nextDispatchR` reset to 0 (safe because their value is stale). Overflow in the subtraction (underflow of unsigned values) is detected and logged.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 5.1 Queue Full Rejection\n\nA request is rejected with `\"queue-full\"` if and only if the selected queue is full **and** the QueueSet is at its concurrency limit simultaneously (`rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked`, line 618). The \"and\" is deliberate: if seats are available, requests are still accepted even if queues are deep, since they can be dispatched immediately. This avoids spurious rejection under bursty load.\n\n**Operational risk**: Misconfigured `QueueLengthLimit` (too low) causes premature rejection under legitimate load spikes. Too high wastes memory and allows unbounded latency accumulation.\n\n### 5.2 Oversized Requests\n\nIf `request.MaxSeats() > ConcurrencyLimit` and other requests are executing, the request cannot be dispatched \u2014 `canAccommodateSeatsLocked` returns false and the dispatch loop stalls. The request waits in its queue. If the request is the *only* thing in the system (`totRequestsExecuting == 0`), it is allowed through anyway to avoid starvation.\n\n**Tradeoff**: This prevents seat arithmetic overflow, but a single oversized request can temporarily block an entire QueueSet.\n\n### 5.3 Virtual Time Windup (Anti-Windup Hack)\n\nA queue that receives no requests for a long time has a stale `nextDispatchR` (from its last dispatch). When it later receives a request, `nextDispatchR` could be far in the past relative to `currentR`, making this queue appear to be owed an enormous amount of service. The anti-windup `boundNextDispatchLocked` (line 952) clamps `nextDispatchR` upward to `oldestWaiting.arrivalR`:\n\n```go\nif queue.nextDispatchR < virtualStartBound {\n    queue.nextDispatchR = virtualStartBound\n}\n```\n\n**Tradeoff**: This is a pragmatic approximation. It prevents windfall service for bursty flows but means a flow that goes idle and returns cannot \"bank\" its unused capacity \u2014 each flow gets at most its fair share going forward.\n\n### 5.4 `estimatedServiceDuration` Is a Fixed Constant\n\n`estimatedServiceDuration` is hardcoded at 3ms (`queueset.go:216`). This estimate is used in:\n\n- Computing `totalWork` for virtual-time bookkeeping (the initial-phase component).\n- Computing `estimatedWorkInProgress` in `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked` (for the `dsMin`/`dsMax` metrics).\n- Post-execution `nextDispatchR` correction: if actual service took 10ms instead of 3ms, `nextDispatchR` is reduced by `7ms * InitialSeats`.\n\n**Risk**: If actual request service times are systematically far from 3ms (e.g., long-running list requests), the virtual-time accounting during queuing is inaccurate. The post-execution correction partially compensates but applies only retroactively.\n\n### 5.5 Borrowing and the `ConcurrencyLimit` Race\n\nThe `ConcurrencyLimit` for a QueueSet is updated every 10 seconds by the borrowing loop via `Complete(DispatchingConfig{ConcurrencyLimit: currentCL})`. `Complete` calls `setConfiguration`, which calls `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` \u2014 meaning the new limit takes effect immediately for dispatch decisions. Between adjustment periods, a priority level with a temporarily lower limit may queue requests that would have been admitted under the old limit.\n\n**Tradeoff**: The 10-second borrowing period provides smoothing (via `seatDemandSmoothingCoefficient = 0.977`, half-life ~5 minutes) against transient load spikes, at the cost of slow adaptation. A sudden traffic surge takes minutes to fully propagate to increased concurrency for a needy level.\n\n### 5.6 `AdditionalLatency` and Deferred Seat Release\n\nWatch requests and large list responses that hold server-side resources after the response headers are sent are modeled with `FinalSeats` and `AdditionalLatency`. The `EventAfterDuration` mechanism schedules seat release asynchronously, so the response is delivered to the client while APF continues to account for the held seats. This correctly models resource consumption but adds complexity:\n\n- A goroutine is spawned per request with non-zero `AdditionalLatency`.\n- Seat release may race with QueueSet reconfiguration.\n- Metrics (`execSeatsGauge`) remain elevated during the additional latency, which is correct but may surprise operators reading dashboards.\n\n### 5.7 Lock Contention\n\nThe entire `queueSet` is protected by a single `sync.Mutex`. Every call to `StartRequest`, `Finish`, and the `EventAfterDuration` callback acquires this lock. Under high request rates this becomes a serialization point. The `syncTimeLocked` call at every lock acquisition advances virtual time \u2014 adding a small but constant overhead proportional to time elapsed.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 6.1 `QueueSetFactory` Interface\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/interface.go:32`\n\nProduction code uses `fqs.NewQueueSetFactory(clk)` (`apf_filter.go:105`). Tests may substitute a `newTestableQueueSetFactory` with a different `promiseFactoryFactory`. The interface is fully replaceable, but in practice the only real implementation is `queueSetFactory` in the `queueset` package.\n\n**Risk**: Replacing the factory is not a supported operator configuration; it requires Go-level code changes.\n\n### 6.2 `promiseFactoryFactory` \u2014 Testability Hook\n\n**File:** `queueset.go:47-54`\n\nThe `promiseFactoryFactory` is a function that, given a `*queueSet`, returns a factory for `WriteOnce` promises. The production factory returns `promise.NewWriteOnce`. Test code can substitute a fake that allows deterministic control of when dispatch decisions are delivered.\n\nThis hook exists purely to make the dispatch-wait race testable without real goroutines and wall-clock time.\n\n### 6.3 `eventclock.Interface` \u2014 Clock Abstraction\n\n**File:** `fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go`\n\nAll time-based operations go through `eventclock.Interface` (which embeds `clock.PassiveClock`). Tests supply a `FakeClock` that controls time and deferred events manually. The real implementation (`eventclock.Real`) wraps standard Go time functions.\n\n**Extension risk**: The clock is wired at `New()` time (`apf_filter.go:94`, `Real{}`). Operators cannot substitute a custom clock without modifying the source.\n\n### 6.4 `WorkEstimator` \u2014 Pluggable Request Sizing\n\n**File:** `request/width.go:75`\n\n`NewWorkEstimator` takes four parameters:\n\n- `objectCountFn` \u2014 returns the stored object count for a resource (used by the list estimator).\n- `watchCountFn` \u2014 returns the number of interested watchers for a request (used by the mutating estimator, which accounts for watch fan-out).\n- `config *WorkEstimatorConfig` \u2014 minimum/maximum seat limits.\n- `maxSeatsFn` \u2014 returns the per-priority-level maximum seats (tracked by `MaxSeatsTracker`, set at 15% of `nominalCL`, `apf_controller.go:63`).\n\nOperators can influence work estimation indirectly through `PriorityLevelConfiguration.spec.limited.limitResponse.queuing` fields and by the object count and watch count functions, which are populated from storage backends.\n\n**Risk**: The work estimator is called while holding `cfgCtlr.lock.RLock()` (inside `startRequest`). A slow `objectCountFn` or `watchCountFn` would hold the read lock and stall all concurrent classification.\n\n### 6.5 `FlowDistinguisherMethod` \u2014 Flow Partitioning\n\n**File:** `apf_controller.go:1115-1129`\n\nThe `flowDistinguisher` fed into hash computation is determined by `DistinguisherMethod.Type`:\n\n- `ByUser` \u2014 uses `rd.User.GetName()`\n- `ByNamespace` \u2014 uses `rd.RequestInfo.Namespace`\n\nThis is the only operator-controlled knob that affects which queue within a priority level a given request lands in. It is set per FlowSchema in the API object. A single-queue priority level ignores it entirely (no shuffle-sharding).\n\n**Tradeoff**: `ByUser` provides isolation between users of the same priority level; `ByNamespace` provides isolation between namespaces. Neither provides isolation across multiple dimensions simultaneously.\n\n### 6.6 `QueueSet.Dump` \u2014 Debug Introspection\n\n**File:** `queueset.go:996`\n\n`Dump(includeRequestDetails bool)` acquires the lock, snapshots all queue state, and returns a `debug.QueueSetDump`. With `includeRequestDetails=true` it also extracts `UserInfo` and `RequestInfo` from the request contexts. This is exposed via the APF debug HTTP endpoint installed by `Install(mux)`.\n\n**Risk**: `Dump` holds the QueueSet lock for the duration of the snapshot. On a large, busy QueueSet this can cause momentary stalls to all concurrent requests.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications\n\n### 7.1 Diagnosing Rejections\n\nThree rejection reasons appear in `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total`:\n\n| Reason | Source | Meaning |\n|---|---|---|\n| `concurrency-limit` | `StartRequest` path A | No-queue priority level hit its seat limit |\n| `queue-full` | `StartRequest` path B | Both queue-length and seat-limit exceeded simultaneously |\n| `time-out` | `request.wait` | Request context cancelled while waiting |\n\n`queue-full` rejections are the primary signal of overload at a priority level. `time-out` rejections indicate clients with short deadlines experiencing sustained queue depth. Neither is necessarily pathological \u2014 some rejection is expected and healthy under overload \u2014 but sustained high rates warrant attention.\n\n### 7.2 Monitoring Virtual Time\n\n`apiserver_flowcontrol_current_r` (set via `metrics.SetCurrentR`) tracks `currentR` per priority level. A monotonically advancing `currentR` indicates the priority level is active. A `currentR` that advances very slowly relative to other levels indicates few active queues or low seat demand.\n\n`apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatch_r`, `apiserver_flowcontrol_latest_s`, and related metrics (set via `metrics.SetDispatchMetrics`) expose `minVirtualFinish`, `sMin`, `sMax`, `dsMin`, `dsMax` from `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`. These are useful for understanding the spread of virtual times across queues \u2014 a large `sMax - sMin` indicates significant imbalance in how much service different flows have received.\n\n### 7.3 Seat Demand and Borrowing Observability\n\n`apiserver_flowcontrol_priority_level_seat_count_samples` tracks the time-weighted integral of seat demand per priority level. The borrowing loop reads this every 10 seconds and adjusts `currentCL`. `apiserver_flowcontrol_lower_limit_seats`, `apiserver_flowcontrol_upper_limit_seats`, and `apiserver_flowcontrol_nominal_limit_seats` expose the bounds within which `currentCL` can move.\n\nIf a priority level is consistently borrowing (its `currentCL` is above its `nominalCL`), other levels are lending it capacity \u2014 verify that the lenders are not starved.\n\n### 7.4 The 3ms Estimation Problem in Practice\n\nBecause `estimatedServiceDuration = 3ms` is fixed, list requests that complete in 500ms inflate a queue's `nextDispatchR` by only `InitialSeats * 3ms` during queuing. The post-execution correction applies after the fact. This means:\n\n- During a queue backup, the virtual-time selection algorithm underestimates the true cost of list requests.\n- Queues containing large lists may be over-dispatched before the correction kicks in.\n- The `WorkEstimate.FinalSeats + AdditionalLatency` portion is accounted correctly in virtual time, since `AdditionalLatency` is a real measured quantity computed by the work estimator from watch fan-out.\n\n### 7.5 Configuration Stability Concerns\n\nEvery change to any `FlowSchema` or `PriorityLevelConfiguration` object triggers a full re-digest of all config objects (`lockAndDigestConfigObjects`). During this re-digest, `cfgCtlr.lock` is held in write mode, blocking all concurrent `startRequest` calls (which need the read lock). This is bounded by informer event rate but can cause brief stalls under heavy automated config churn (e.g., frequent operator or controller writes).\n\nWhen `DesiredNumQueues` decreases, excess queues are not discarded immediately \u2014 they drain by attrition (`removeQueueIfEmptyLocked`). During draining, the queue count exceeds `DesiredNumQueues`, which means shuffle-sharding deals from more queues than configured, slightly reducing isolation guarantees until all excess queues are empty.\n\n### 7.6 Memory Budget\n\nEach `queue` holds a `requestFIFO` of waiting `*request` values plus a `sets.Set[*request]` of executing ones. With `N` priority levels each having `Q` queues and `L` max queue length, the worst-case waiting-request memory is `N * Q * L * sizeof(request)`. A `request` struct carries its context, work estimate, and two `interface{}` descriptors \u2014 roughly 200\u2013400 bytes depending on context size. For typical APF configs (e.g., 64 queues, 50-item limit), this is negligible, but operators who configure very large queue depths should account for memory usage under pathological overload.\n\n---\n\n## 8. File Map\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_filter.go                    Interface definition, Handle() entry point,\n\u2502 ## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries

### Purpose

The APF (API Priority and Fairness) QueueSet subsystem implements **Fair Queuing for Server Requests** inside the Kubernetes API server. Its job is to prevent any single client or flow from monopolizing the apiserver's concurrency budget, while still making forward progress for all active flows under overload.

Every non-exempt apiserver request is routed through a *priority level*, each of which owns exactly one `QueueSet`. The `QueueSet` for a priority level is the gate that decides:

- whether an incoming request can be dispatched immediately (seats available),
- whether it must wait in a queue (backpressure),
- whether it must be rejected outright (queue full and concurrency limit exceeded), or
- whether it times out while waiting (context cancelled).

### Scope Boundary

The QueueSet subsystem is responsible only for **queuing and dispatch decisions** within a single priority level. It has no knowledge of:

- how requests are classified (FlowSchema matching happens in `apf_controller.go`);
- cross-level concurrency borrowing (also handled at the controller layer);
- HTTP-level admission or request
... (truncated)
